3:05 Ocean City, MD....
If anyone wants to import a car from Germany look at the local climate it's coming from. Despite its relatively small size Germany's climate in winter varies a lot and thus the amount of salt the cars are exposed to. Also city cars are usually less rusty. The best would probably from the Cologne area. Very little frost and very very rare snow events. In urban areas even less so.
If it has 4wd or a G-Lader in the description - consider how likely your kid was really gonna graduate anyway..  Edit: Golf wearing BBS will always be solid.

James, think about this (this is basically the project i finished...and sold when my kid was born, so i could have a bigger car, also project at the moment :D) : 2008 polo, 1.4tdi .  Sounds crazy to modify them, but it's incredibly  rewarding and quite unique. Had the BNM engine (keep away from BMS code) , 70 hp. Changed injectors(AL code), fitted bigger turbo(1749VA), strongflex all around except dogbone (would'v rattle like crazy with that), changed the seats to red leather alfa 147, JDD gearbox with axles and mounts(stock has a tiny disk and low ratios -192kmph topspeed. JDD has the tallest of them -260kmph topspeed ).  Ended up at 149.9 hp and 341 nm...good amount of torque steer and smiles. This build costs pennies, it's simple to do and it's sooo different from anything else.  These (modified) are very rare in EU also, but i dont think you would find any in the US...plus great mpg (i was averaging around 5-6L/100km, that's about 40-50mpg). If you want pics or info, just contact me :D. I did all my research and the fella that tuned it is the same that has the current WR for 402m on this engine ...11s, 290hp+nos  (you can search for "blue arosa")  Also, good job with the channel! The VW Golf/GTi is effectively the Ford Mustang of Europe.  It has the same level of aftermarket support as Mustangs and Jeeps.  Sure a Honda Civic has a lot of aftermarket support too, but a lot of the parts you find for Civics are "universal fitment".  With the VW Golf/GTi, Ford Mustang and Jeep (you know which one) the majority of the aftermarket parts are specific parts with specific fitments for specific model years.  There is very little "universal fitment".

NordVPN is a security risk. In order to scan your media 'on the fly' for malware it has to decrypt the HTTPS TLS tunnel that already exists between you and the websites server. How does it do this? By having you install their certificate on your system, then performing a transparent proxy man in the middle attack on your connection. To the server they pretend to be you, to you they pretend to be the webserver. They decrypt your data, scan it, reencrypt it and send it to you. By the way, they also collect metrics on what they scan to sell to advertisers.   DO NO TRUST A COMPANY THAT BLATANTLY COMPROMISES YOUR SECURITY...ESPECIALLY WHEN ITS A SECURITY COMPANY!!! NordVPN lies to you. Do not trust them. At all. Period.

Word of advice to any youngsters who are wanting to get into the community just know the V.A.G. enthusiasts are like a family. We don't care how quick or fast your car is or whether or not you can destroy tires. We are all about the little details like period correct wheels, OEM+, clean or hard to find accessories. James, Do you know what the K wire is? I learned the hard way after a stereo install on my Cabrio and my car wouldn't pass smog. it's a brown 9v line that runs on a seperate system than the 12v system. I had bad eye and thought it was a black wire but it was dark brown, ended up splicing with the ground wire. Turns out it was a communication line for the EMS. Anyway, something to think of! Cheers!

advice for your channel: talk less, do more!
I think one point in the intro of the video is really far fetched. The car you showed, when you said 'replicated' was a project by the biggest automotive oriented channel in Germany: 'JP Performance'. It really has nothing to to with an ordinary Golf other than some parts of the outer shell. The chassis i a completely custom build tubeframe, fabricated by an aerospace company in Germany. Its heart is a V10 from an Audi R8 wich is also twin turboed. I know, that not everyone knows their stuff, but they are also recognized in the US and had cars at SEMA '23 and '24 ('23: VW Beetle with a 5 cyl and 1 of 1 body kit. '24: VW Golf 2, inspired by renderings from Kyza, the "Thunderbunny", rear mid-engine VR6)  So no, they didnt replicate your Golf. But they do pretty awesome stuff, even besides building cars like a car museum, a private race track, Clothing, Burgers, etc.  But maybe an episode on them would be nice.  EDIT: If you're interested in what they are doing, there are some awesome videos from Larry Chen and some old Hoonigan episodes with Scotto, Vin, etc. when they visited germany to buy cars.

My guy, the amount of rust on that car is nominal at worst. They make replacement aftermarket rockers, quarter panels, fenders, hoods, door skins, rooftops and just about every other body panel. Talk to a guy who has been rebuilding old muscle cars in the Northeast and they would probably laugh at you for saying that amount of rust would total out that car. have you seen the shape of some of those old muscle cars that get completely restored? Some of them are barely two windshield frames and a seat anymore but a few years later they come out looking better than the day they rolled off the factory floors. As for your engine I'm willing to say you probably toasted at least two of the rod bearings. If you were smart you would have immediately shut it down as soon as you heard the ticking sound to save from doing damage to any other parts but at this point I'm guessing you have probably scored the crank pretty well and quite possibly warped a rod or two. You're better off keeping the car, replacing the panels and just buying an entire new engine considering they are only 500 bucks or whatever you said...

The downside (or upside if you love fixing stuff) of these cars is that everything breaks all of the fucking time. I don't mind working on my stuff every month but every weekend was exhausting to the point that I had to switch back to JDM stuff. All in all, I would rate my VW experience a 6.5/10 and I would recommend getting into it

5-cylinder engines are such a hidden gem. Equally enthusiastic to VW are the Volvo owners on the P1, 5-cyl platform. The C30 hatchback and V50/V60 wagons were bona-fide turbo rippers with over 230hp stock, and the S40 sedan was a great daily for the normies. They came in stick and AWD variants too, and many components were Ford MC crossover, meaning parts aren't really all that crazy to find. Good to see the love.

8:40 "Community" This is so underrated. Not just the Golf, Volkswagens in general. Car scenes tend to be really cliquey with people staying around others in their niche, but VW has just been wholly different. I met some of my best friends and some of the weirdest assortment of people in general because of Volkswagens. Relators, Mechanics, Rally drivers, bankers, trades guys, retail, sales, hell even a local politician. You got your GTI hotboys, Old school MK1/2 guys who have been there for decades. The Van and Beetle hippies, The niche VW SUV overlanders. The people with stock VWs who are just as welcome and part of the club as the super modified Golf and mint collector Van people. The community is next level.  I moved to a new city and on the drive I had my exhaust get ripped off in a construction zone. Posted in the local VW Facebook group that I had just arrived in town and had nowhere to fix. Had multiple replies in minutes with driveways and tools I could use. The guy who's house I rolled up to let me use his tools, helped me crawl around under the car, even hooked me up with some Audi summer wheels and tires so I could get off my winter tires. For free. I had just met him.

As a former MK3 owner, I do miss mine, but I do not miss how poor handling of a car it was, even with modifications.  They're profoundly front-heavy, and have terrible suspension geometry.  The suspension can't be lowered without introducing lots of bump-steer, and the geometry of the suspension compressing affects the camber too much.  I tried to make one into an Autocross car, and it was a lost cause.  Honda Civics ran circles around me with much less work done to them.
